### Post by Admir_Zatega on 2015-09-25
I have windows and Ubuntu on my pc.
I only gave 20GB to Ubuntu while installing, and I started running out of space.
So I shrunk the windows partition, and expanded the Ubuntu one.
The ubuntu partition was moved left, now when I try to boot into ubuntu I get this error:

    unable to launch "gnome-session --session=ubuntu" X session ---
    "gnome-session --session=ubuntu" not found; falling back to default session.

Thanks :)

I hope my pc isn't doomed to windows :P:lolflag:

---

### Post by sudodus on 2015-09-25
Welcome to the Ubuntu Forums :-)

When you move a system partition's head end, the bootloader won't find it. You need to boot from a live drive (DVD/USB), for example the Ubuntu install drive, and re-install the bootloader. See this link

[Grub2/Installing#Fixing_a_Broken_System](https://help.ubuntu.com/community/Grub2/Installing#Fixing_a_Broken_System)

---

### Post by sudodus on 2015-09-25
- Does it boot after treatment with boot-repair? 

Don't worry too much about the text in the grub menu, the important thing is if it works or not.

- Was there a kali system in the computer before or is there such a system alongside Ubuntu?

- What version is it (that you try to make bootable again) - some special version of Ubuntu, for example a community re-spin, or is it standard Ubuntu?

### Post by sudodus on 2015-09-25
This is strange. How did you install Ubuntu: 

- What medium (DVD or USB)?

- What tool?

- Did it work before you changed the partition size?

-o-

What error output is there? Is it stiil this one:

> unable to launch "gnome-session --session=ubuntu" X session ---
"gnome-session --session=ubuntu" not found; falling back to default session.

Then it boots, but is corrupted. Maybe you can restore it with the following command, when booted from another drive, I suggest the live drive

Identify the drive letter and partition number of the root partition of the installed system. If you need help, please post the output of the following commands (in a terminal window), also when you have booted from the same other drive

```
sudo lsblk -fm
```
```
df
```

Then run the following command which can repair file system errors (if that is the cause of your problem)

```
sudo e2fsck -f /dev/sdxy
```

where x is the drive letter and y is the partition number (maybe /dev/sdb5, but use what you find out from the lsblk and df commands)

---

### Post by sudodus on 2015-09-27
Now whatever you do, please ***take a backup of all the files that you want to keep***. The following operation may fail, and I want you to keep the important files, whatever happens.

Then you can re-install. Select 'Something else' at the partitioning page. Then install the system into the same root partition and ***do not format*** the drive. (If you format the drive, your data will be wiped.)

---

### Post by sudodus on 2015-09-28
Please tell us about your graphics card/chip!

Did you use a proprietary graphics driver before? In that case, try to install the same driver again.

Maybe you can use ***xrandr*** to modify the resolution? What resolution should there be, and what is it now?

Please post the output of ```
xrandr
```

### Post by sudodus on 2015-09-28
It might be possible to solve each of your problems, but it is probably faster and easier to make a fresh installation and copy back your personal files from the backup.

The only reason (but it might be a good one) to continue to repair is that you learn a lot about your system that way :-)

### Post by sudodus on 2015-09-28
It is valuable for the community to exchange ideas in the forum except in very special situations. There are PMs, but they are not really faster.

You can also join some IRC forum, which is faster. Some people prefer that. Try it. That is also where we can find some developers.

See at the top of this page: the pulldown menu ***Other support -- Ubuntu IRC chat***
